Jamison Brereton

132
Indra
Paruchepa Daivod─Бsi
6 verses: atyaс╣гс╣нi
This short hymn contains many puzzles of detail, which render much of the trans lation provisional, but the general theme is fairly clear. The present time and the current sacrifice are repeatedly highlighted (see, e.g., vss. 1тАУ2), and the contrast between now and the past is explicitly drawn (see vss. 3тАУ4). As is usual when past

and present are invoked together, we ask Indra to aid us in the same way as he aided his companions in myth, particularly, here, the Aс╣Еgirases at the opening of the Vala cave (vs. 4). The theme of speech, both by and about Indra, is also strongly high lighted, especially in the first four verses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Possessed of) former opulence, Maghavan, (through your bounty); protected, Indra, by you, may we overcome those who are arrayed in (hostile) hoste; may we anticipate (our) assailants. (The sacrifice) of today being nigh, speak encouragingly to the presenter of the libation; may we bring together at this rite (suitable offerings and praises) to you, the victor in war; worshipping you, the victor in war.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bhare kс╣Ыtam = saс╣Еgr─Бme jayasya kart─Бram; bhara iti saс╣Еgr─Бman─Бma, bharaterv─Б haraterv─Б (Nirukta 4.24)

Jamison Brereton

With you, bounteous Indra, aided by you, may we overcome those who do battle over the foremost stakesтАФmay we win against those who
seek to win.
On this, the nearest day speak on behalf of the soma-presser.
At this sacrifice may we pull out the perfect (тАЬhandтАЭ of dice) at the
matchтАФseeking the prize, (may we pull out) the perfect one at
the match.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the published translation I treat the first member of the three-member cmpd ├нndratvot─Бс╕е as if it were a voc., since the lit. тАЬaided by you, IndraтАЭ seems clumsy.

The verb ├бdhi voc─Б could also be a 1st sg. subj., but with most tr. I take it as 2nd sg. impv.; тАЬIтАЭ am a less likely advocate for the presser than Indra is.

With Geldner I consider v├н cayema bh├бre kс╣Ыt├бm (f) a gambling expression; for another such expression see the previous hymn, I.131.5d.

Griffith

HELPED, Indra Maghavan, by thee in war of old, may we subdue in fight the men who strive with us, conquer the men who war with us.
This day that now is close at hand bless him who pours the Soma juice.
In this our sacrifice may we divide the spoil, showing our strength, the spoil of war.

Geldner

Mit dir, du Gabenreicher, wollen wir im Kampf um den ersten Preis, mit deinem Beistand, o Indra, die Gegner besiegen, wollen wir die Eifers├╝chtigen ├╝bertrumpfen. An diesem n├дchsten Tage entscheide doch ja zu Gunsten des Somaopfernden. Bei diesem Opfer wollen wir den h├╢chsten Wurf im Gewinnspiel aussuchen, nach dem Siegerpreis strebend den h├╢chsten Wurf im Gewinnspiel.

Grassmann

Durch dich, o m├дchtiger, m├╢gen wir in dem alten Kampfe, von dir, o Indra, unterst├╝tzt die Feinde besiegen, ├╝berwinden die bek├дmpfenden; an diesem n├дchsten Tage m├╢gest du nun dem Somapresser Muth einsprechen; bei diesem Opfer m├╢gen wir die im Kampf gemachte Beute vertheilen, wir nach Gut verlangenden die im Kampf gemachte Beute.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn the combat which secures heaven, Indra, (treading) in the appropriate and straight path of the active (combatant), as well as in his own appropriate and straight (path), destroys (the adversary) of him who wakes at dawn and celebrates (pious rites); he therefore to be adored with the head (bowed down), as revernce is paid by prostration to a holy sage. May your treasures, (Indra), be accusative ulated upon us; may the treasures of you who are auspicious be auspicious (to us).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Svasminna├▒jasi, are the words reiterated;

Vakma = vakmani, own, peculiar;

M─Бrge = in the road or path, i.e. honest, straight, free from fraud, kapaс╣н─Бdirahite or open, unconcaled, apracchanne

Jamison Brereton

At the match to win the sun, at the speech of the Propitiator, at the very anointing of the one who wakes at dawn [=Agni]тАФat the very
anointing of the one being prepared [=soma]тАФ
on (that) day Indra is to be invoked by every head [=person], in the way that is known.
Toward us only let your gifts be directedтАФthe auspicious gifts of the auspicious one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бdas abc consist entirely of four locative expressions (with their genitives); this heavily signposted syntactic pattern allows (/forces) the first word of d, ├бhan(n) to be interpreted as the loc. sg. of ├бhar тАШdayтАЩ rather than the 2nd/3rd sg. root impf. of тИЪhan, which otherwise would be strongly favored in an Indra context. (Note that the identical opening, ├бhann ├нndro, is found at IV.28.3, with the verb.) The locatives in 1d, f also reinforce the loc. reading, esp. asm├нn ├бhani (1d). I donтАЩt know exactly what to call this poetic trick – it is aggressively a non-pun.

─Бpr├б- in a is a hapax, and there is no consensus on its meaning or derivation; see EWA s.v. I am inclined to follow Geldner (etc.)тАЩs connection with ─Бpr─л╠Б- (a noun that doesn’t occur in the RV, though the verbal syntagm does) with a meaning тАШpropitiatorтАЩ vel sim. This fits its dependence on v├бkmani тАШat the speechтАЩ and may also thematically echo ├бdhi voc─Б тАШadvocate, speak on behalf ofтАЩ in 1e. It could indeed refer to the reciter of ─Аpr─л hymns. The other leading etymological candidate is ─Б╠БтИЪpс╣Ы тАШfillтАЩ (so Witzel Got┼Н; see Oldenberg), but тАЬthe fillerтАЭ seems to have less connection with speaking than тАЬthe propitiator.тАЭ The way the reflexive adj. sv├бsmin works in bc is a little tricky: тАЬof X, at his very own anointing.тАЭ On the basis of I.134.2 I follow Geldner in taking kr─Бс╣З├бsya as passive and referring to the soma. Thus in bc we find the anointing (├б├▒jasi) of the two primary ritual substances, fire (b) and soma (c). Alternatively, if it seems desirable to keep the referent the same in the two p─Бdas, one can follow Renou, Witzel Got┼Н in taking kr─Бс╣З├б- as тАЬactive,тАЭ referring to Agni.

The use of тАШheadтАЩ (┼Ы├нras-/┼Ы─лrс╣г├бn-) to refer to an individual person is not, as far as I know, otherwise found in the RV, though the semantic dev. is obvious and precedented in English.

Griffith

In war which wins the light, at the free-giver’s call, at due oblation of the early-rising one, oblation of the active one,
Indra slew, even as we know–whom each bowed head must reverence.
May all thy bounteous gifts be gathered up for us, yea, the good gifts of thee the Good.

Geldner

Im Kampf, wenn es gilt das Sonnenlicht zu gewinnen, bei der Rede des F├╝rbitters, wenn der fr├╝hwache Agni seine Salbung bekommt, wenn der angemachte Soma seine Salbung bekommt; an dem Tage ist Indra, wie bekannt, Haupt f├╝r Haupt anzurufen. Auf uns sollen sich deine Gaben vereinigen, die gl├╝ckbringenden Gaben des Gl├╝ckbringenden.

Grassmann

In dem glanzverschaffenden Kampfe, bei dem Rufe des eifrigen, bei der eignen Ausschm├╝ckung des fr├╝h wachen [Agni], bei der eignen Ausschm├╝ckung des wirksamen; Indra erschlug [die Feinde] nach seiner Weise, er der von jedem Wesen anzurufen ist; bei uns m├╢gen sein deine Gaben allesammt, des heilbringenden heilbringende Gaben.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! (рдпрдерд╛) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рд╕рдзреНрд░реНрдпрдХреН) рд╕рд╛рде рдЬрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдордгреНрдбрд▓ (рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЬреЗрд╖реЗ) рд╕реБрдЦ рд╕реЗ рдЬреАрддрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╡рд┐рджреЗ) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖реНрдгрд╛рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖реНрдгрд╛) рд╢рд┐рд░ рдорд╛рдереЗ (рдЙрдкрд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдпрдГ) рд╕рдореАрдк рдХрд╣рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рднрд░реЗ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдо рдореЗрдВ (рдЖрдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдп) рдкреВрд░реНрдг рдмрд▓ (рдХреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╕реНрдп) рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╕рдордп рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧ (рдЙрд╖рд░реНрдмреБрдзрдГ) рдЙрд╖рдГрдХрд╛рд▓ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐ рдХреЗ рдЪреМрдереЗ рдкреНрд░рд╣рд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЬрд╛рдЧреЗ рд╣реБрдП рддреБрдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд╡рдХреНрдордирд┐) рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдореЗрдВ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) рдЕрдкрдиреЗ (рдЕрдЮреНрдЬрд╕рд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдХреЗ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрдд рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) рдЕрдкрдиреЗ (рдЕрдЮреНрдЬрд╕рд┐) рдЪрд╛рд╣реЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдореЗрдШ рдХреЛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдп (рдЕрд╣рдиреН) рдорд╛рд░рддрд╛ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдорд╛рд░реЛ, рдЬреЛ (рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрд░рд╛) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдмреАрдЪ (рднрджреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд░рд╛рддрдпрдГ) рджрд╛рди рдЖрджрд┐ рдХрд╛рдо (рддреЗ) рддреБрдо (рднрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп) рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреЗ (рд░рд╛рддрдпрдГ) рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╣реЛрдВ рд╡реЗ (рддреЗ) рддреЗрд░реЗ (рд╕рдиреНрддреБ) рд╣реЛрдВ рее реи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛ рдФрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИрдВред рдЬреЛ рд╕рднрд╛рдкрддрд┐ рд╕рдм рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬреАрддрдХрд░ рд╕рдмрдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рджреЗ рд╕рдХрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдо рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рдФрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдФрд░ рдФрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗред рдРрд╕реЗ рдПрдХ рджреВрд╕рд░реЗ рдореЗрдВ рдкреНрд░реАрддрд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдз рдЫреЛрдбрд╝ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдЬрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее реи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рд╕рдзреНрд░реНрдпрдЧрд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЬреЗрд╖реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреЗ рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖реНрдгрд╛рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖реНрдгреЛрдкрд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╕реНрддрдерд╛ рднрд░реЗ рдЖрдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдХреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╕реНрдпреЛрд╖рд░реНрдмреБрдзреЛ рд╡рдХреНрдордирд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирдЮреНрдЬрд╕реАрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирдЮреНрдЬрд╕рд┐ рдореЗрдШрдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛрд╜рд╣рдиреНрдирд┐рд╡ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдШреНрдирдиреНрддреБ рдпрд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрд░рд╛ рднрджреНрд░рд╛ рд░рд╛рддрдпрд╕реНрддреЗ рднрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд░рд╛рддрдп рдЗрд╡ рд╕реНрдпреБрд╕реНрддрд╛рд╕реНрддреЗ рд╕рдиреНрддреБ рее реи рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЬреЗрд╖реЗ) рд╕реБрдЦреЗрди рдЬрдпрд╢реАрд▓рд╛рдп (рднрд░реЗ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рдЖрдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдп) рдкреВрд░реНрдгрдмрд▓рд╕реНрдп (рд╡рдХреНрдордирд┐) рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢реЗ (рдЙрд╖рд░реНрдмреБрдзрдГ) рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдердкреНрд░рд╣рд░реЗ рдЬрд╛рдЧреГрддрд╛рдГ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) (рдЕрдЮреНрдЬрд╕рд┐) рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯреЗ (рдХреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╕реНрдп) рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд╕реНрдпред рдЕрд╡ рд╡рд╛ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реАрддрд┐ рд╢рдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХреНред (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) (рдЕрдЮреНрдЬрд╕рд┐) рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдиреЗ (рдЕрд╣рдиреН) рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ (рдпрдерд╛) (рд╡рд┐рджреЗ) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рддреЗ (рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖реНрдгрд╛ рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖реНрдгрд╛) рд╢рд┐рд░рд╕рд╛ рд╢рд┐рд░рд╕рд╛ (рдЙрдкрд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдпрдГ) рдЙрдкрд╡рдХреНрддреБрдВ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдГ (рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрд░рд╛) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рд╕реБ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╕рдзреНрд░реНрдпрдХреН) рд╕рд╣рд╛рд╜рдЮреНрдЪрддреАрддрд┐ (рд╕рдиреНрддреБ) рднрд╡рдиреНрддреБ (рд░рд╛рддрдпрдГ) рджрд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ (рднрджреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдХрд░рд╛рдГ (рднрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп) рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдХрд░рд╕реНрдп (рд░рд╛рддрдпрдГ) рджрд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ рее реи рее

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реМред рдпрд╕реНрд╕рднреЗрд╢рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдиреН рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╕рддреНрд╕рддреНрдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ рд╕ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЬрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрднреНрдпрдГ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рджрд╛рддреБрдВ рд╢рдХреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрд╛рдГ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдЪ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдГ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдПрд╡рдВ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдкреНрд░реАрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдзрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдп рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдГ рее реи рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, in whatsoever rite (the priests) from of old have plural ced the brilliant (sacrificial) food for you upon the altar, in that plural ce of sacrifice you abide; do you declare what (rite), that men may thence behold the intermediate (firmament bright) with the rays (of the sun); for this, Indra, the searcher (of rain, is) the searcher after cattle, for (the benefit of) his kindred (worshippers), and knows in due course (the season of the rain).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъtasya v─Бrasi kс╣гayam yaj├▒asya niv─Бsasth─Бnam saс╣Гbhaktosi, you are possessed o fthe plural ce of the abode of the sacrifice, termed с╣Ыta, or the true, as giving unfailing reward; or с╣Ыta = water; i.e. you abide in the dwelling of the water = sender of rain, vс╣Ыс╣гс╣нiprado asi; another interpretation: с╣Ыta meaning the sun, you cause (the sacrificer) to go to the region of the sun. sa gh─Б vide anvindro gaveс╣гaс╣Зa bandhukс╣гidbhyo gaveс╣гaс╣Зaс╕е = lit. he verily knows in order, Indra, the searcher, gaveс╣гaс╣Зa; udakasy─Бnveс╣гaс╣Зa- ┼Ы─лlaс╕е, possessed of or practising the seeking after water, the sender of rain; gav─Бm eс╣гaс╣Зakart─Б, the maker of search after the cows, alluding to the old legend; or, it may mean: the seeker for the reward of the worshipper, yajam─Бna- phalasya mс╣Ыgayit─Б; vide, anuvide: he knows in order, is filled up by udakapr─Бptiprak─Бram, he understands the manifestation of the attainemnt or arrival, in due season, of the rains

Jamison Brereton

This pleasurable offering of yours is glittering as of old, when at the sacrifice they [=sacrificers] made (you), the shield, as a peaceful
dwelling for themselvesтАФyou are the shield of truth, a peaceful
dwelling.
You should announce this now yet again. They [=poets?] look within (themselves?) with the (coming of) the (sunтАЩs) rays [=dawn].
тАЬThis Indra is certainly known as a seeker of cowsтАФas a seeker of cows for those who dwell among their kindred.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

A very opaque verse, which has received multiple interpretations. I will discuss only my own, very tentative, one here.

I take p─Бda a as the announcement to Indra of the тАЬpleasurable offeringтАЭ (pr├бyaс╕е) currently set out for him at this sacrifice (asm├нn yaj├▒├й 1f); see nearby I.134.1, 135.4 for similar usage of pr├бyas-. This glittering offering reminds the poet of a previous one (pratn├бth─Б). I take the next two p─Бdas (bc) as describing this previous one; the relative locative y├бsmin yaj├▒├й is a temporal expression that picks up the temporal pratn├бth─Б.

The crux in bc is the pair v─Б╠Бram (b), v─Б╠Бr (c). Since the former is an obj. of ├бkс╣Ыс╣Зvata and the latter a (possible) subj. of ├бsi, an analysis as a masc. (or at least gendered) root noun suggests itself, but such a noun has at best a precarious existence (see Schindler WurNom s.v.). Nonetheless, I think it must be posited here; the other solutions, which include taking the two forms to two separate stems (see, e.g., Grassmann, Lubotsky) or decomposing them into v─Б + aтАж (Hoffmann apud Schindler, Witzel Got┼Н), do too much violence to the patterns of Atyaс╣гс╣нi meter. With Geldner and Renou in their separate ways (тАЬSchirmer(?)тАЭ тАЬprotecteurтАЭ) I take the form to тИЪvс╣Ы тАШcoverтАЩ and tr.

тАШshieldтАЩ (as in X.93.3). In b this noun in the acc. is in apposition to unexpressed tv─Б тАШyouтАЩ, i.e., Indra – which is the first obj. to a double acc. тИЪkс╣Ы construction тАШmake X into YтАЩ. (For Indra as a home, see 5fg. For kс╣г├бya- in a metaphorical sense, see the next hymn, I.133.7a.) In the tag-p─Бda the construction has been switched from acc. to nom., and the 2nd sg. ref. is now overt (asi тАШyou areтАЩ). A nom. v─Б╠Бr conforms to this case switch; however, since kс╣г├бya- is masc., we should expect *kс╣г├бyaс╕е here. I explain the anomaly by the pressures of Atyaс╣гс╣нi, which requires strict identity between the finals of b and c; kс╣г├бyam is simply repeated from b or made an honorary neut. for the occasion. It is possible to avoid this problem by assuming that v─Б╠Бr- has verbal rection (so implicitly Geldner тАЬder Schirmer(?) des HausesтАЭ; see also Schindler WurNom), but this introduces further complications, and I prefer the double acc. interpr. anyway.

If bc refers to a time in the distant past when Indra was made into our protector, d may then call for the restatement of this fact at the current ritual (depicted in p─Бda a by my interpr.) The expression n┼л╠Бitth─Б╠Бte p┼лrv├бth─Б ca prav─Б╠Бcyam тАЬNow in the current way and in the earlier one it is to be proclaimed of youтАЭ in 4a supports my interpr of the larger stucture of this verse, namely that it concerns the conceptual intersection of the current ritual and the previous one and that what has been said before needs to be restated at the current sacrifice. Note also that, though the form of тИЪvac, voceс╕е in this case, now has the preverb v├н, the sequence vocer ├бdha, with the adv. ├бdha, echoes ├бdhi voc─Б in 1e.

In e I take ra┼Ыm├нbhiс╕е as a temporal expression тАЬwith the rays (of the sun),тАЭ identifying the time as dawn, as is very common. The standard tr. take it as an instr.

of the means of seeing; this is not impossible, but seems less idiomatic. See further ad I.135.3.

I donтАЩt quite know what to do with ├бnu in f, but given the other difficulties in the verse, this is a minor problem.

Griffith

This food glows for thee as of old at sacrifice, wherein they made thee chooser of the place, for thou choosest the place of sacrifice.
Speak thou and make it known to us: they see within with beams of light.
Indra, indeed, is found a seeker after spoil, spoil-seeker for his own allies.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour exploits, Indra, are worthy to be glorified; now, verily, as well as in former times, when you did open the cloud for the Aс╣Еgirasas, restoring to them their cattle–conquer for us, fight for us, as you did for them; humble in behalf of those who present libations, him who offers no worship; him who rages against us, and offers no worship.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vrajam = a cloud; in the second repetition, the cattle of the Aс╣Еgirasas, stolen by Paс╣Зi; hence, vrajam = a cow-pen or pasture

Jamison Brereton

Now in the current way and in the earlier one it is to be proclaimed of you, that you opened up the enclosure for the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАФo Indra,
doing your best, (you opened) up the enclosure.
In the same way as for them, win and fight for us.
For those who press soma, weaken anyone who follows no
commandmentтАФwho follows no commandment, even when he rages.

Griffith

So now must thy great deed be lauded as of old, when for the Angirases thou openedst the stall, openedst, giving aid, the stall.
In the same manner for us here fight thou and be victorious:
To him who pours the juice give up the lawless man, the lawless who is wroth with us.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInasmuch as the hero (indra), rightly judges men by their deeds, therefore do the (pious), sacrificing (to him) for sustenance, become enabled, by the wealth that has been attained, to overcome (their foes); desirous of food, they diligently worship (him); the (sacrificial) food offered to him in the source of progeny (to the worshipper), and (men) worship him, that by their own strength they may overcome (their foes); pious sacrificers enjoy residence in the heaven of Indra; pious sacrificers are, as it were, in the presence of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъravasyavaс╕е, plural of ┼Ыravasyu = from vb. ┼Ыravasya; ┼Ыravas, food or fame, a wish or desire for food or fame; first occurrence: ’they, desirous of food’; second occurrence: ‘desirous of offering food’ oblations to Indra. In the heaven of Indra: the text has only indre, in Indra; i.e. in the abode or vicinity of Indra; an example of metonymy: gaс╣Еg─Бy─Бm ghoс╣гaс╕е, a village in or on the Ganga, i.e. on the banks of the Ganga

Jamison Brereton

When the champion makes the peoples see in accord with his
conceptions, seeking fame they will surpass when the prize is setтАФ
seeking fame they will distinguish themselves.
To him they chant, for him to thrust (to them) with his strength a (full) lifetime along with offspring.
In Indra do our thoughts desire to establish their homeтАФour thoughts (going) as if to the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For ─лkс╣г├бyat see Jamison 1983: 123. It has the same double I/T value I also ascribe to cit├бyanta(с╕е) in I.131.2f.

In de I take b─Б╠Бdhe as an infinitive with t├бsmai [=Indra] as subj. and ─Б╠Бyuс╕е praj─Б╠Бvat as obj. This requires тИЪb─Бdh to have a positive value (тАШthrust [s.th. good] towards [s.o.]тАЩ), rather than the usual negative тАШthrust away, repelтАЩ, but see I.61.2 for a similar positive sense.

Griffith

When with wise plan the Hero leads the people forth, they conquer in the ordered battle, seeking fame, press, eager, onward seeking fame.
To him in time of need they sing for life with offspring and with strength.
Their hymns with Indra find a welcome place of rest: the hymns go forward to the Gods.

Geldner

Wenn der Held die Augen aller Leute nebst ihren Gedanken auf sich zieht, dann suchen sich bei ausgesetztem Kampfpreis die Ehrgeizigen zu ├╝berbieten, zeichnen sich die Ehrgeizigen aus. Ihm preisen sie nach Kr├дften ein langes kinderreiches Leben an, um ihn zu best├╝rmen. Die frommen Gedanken m├╢chten sich bei Indra eine Heimst├дtte bereiten; wie sich┬┤s zu den G├╢ttern ziemt, gehen die frommen Gedanken zu ihm.

Wenn der Held durch seine Geisteskr├дfte die Menschen erleuchtet, dann k├дmpfen bei ausgesetztem Preise siegreich die schatzbegierigen, dann dringen vor die schatzbegierigen; ihm singen sie mit Kraft, um kinderreiches Alter st├╝rmend zu erlangen; in ihm suchen die Gebete ihre Heimatsst├дtte, wie zu den G├╢ttern hin die Gebete.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra and Parvata, who are foremost in battles, slay every one who is arrayed against us; slay every such (adversary) with the thunderbolt–(the shaft that) bent upon his destruction pursues him, however far, or to whatever hiding plural ce he may have fled. You, hero, (tear) our enemies entirely to pieces; the tearer (of foes, the thunderbolt), rends them entirely asunder.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Parvata = a cloud, or the deity presiding over clouds, another form of Indra

Jamison Brereton

You two, Indra and тАЬMountainтАЭ [=mace], who fight in the frontтАФ whoever would give battle to us, smash that very one awayтАФwith a
mace smash that very one. (Under these circumstances, even) an abyss will be pleasing to (that one,) who has fled into the distanceтАФan abyss he will seek to reach.
O champion, (surround) our rivals all around on all sidesтАФlet the
splitter split (them) on all sides.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The dual dvandva indr─Б-parvat─Б тАШIndra and MountainтАЩ raises the question of the identity of тАШMountainтАЩ; as in III.53.1 I think it is a designation of IndraтАЩs mace (v├бjra). That the mace shows up in the instr. in the same p─Бda as the dual verb that has Indra and Parvata as implicit subj. (c v├бjreс╣Зa тАж hatam) does not, I think, rule out this interpr.: as тАЬMountainтАЭ the mace is animatized; in the instrumental it is an inanimate instrument.

The t├бm of p─Бda a is an anticipatory placeholder for t├бс╣Г-tam ├нd in b, c.

Renou and Witzel Got┼Н take chantsat (тИЪchand) in d as meaning тАШappearтАЩ: тАЬthere will appear a g├бhanam for him тАжтАЭ – that is, тАШcome into view, take shapeтАЩ. But though тАШappearтАЩ in modern European lgs. can cover that sense, the тАШappearтАЩ sense of тИЪchand is generally тАШhave the appearance of, look likeтАЩ. GeldnerтАЩs interpr. is more complex: he takes the v├бjra- to be the underlying subject, which to the fugitive will look like a g├бhanam. This interpr. represents the sense of тИЪchand better, but at the cost of producing something close to nonsense, at least as I tried to understand it. I instead use the developed sense тАШbe pleasingтАЩ of тИЪchand: the point is that once Indra and Parvata start smiting him, even falling into an abyss will be preferable.

Griffith

Indra and Parvata, our champions in the fight, drive ye away each man who fain would war with us, drive him far from us with the bolt.
Welcome to him concealed afar shall he the lair that he hath found.
So may the Render rend our foes on every side, rend them, O Hero, everywhere.

Geldner

Indra und Parvata, schlaget ihr beide als Vork├дmpfer jeden weg, der uns anfeinden sollte, mit der Keule erschlaget jeden! Dem in der Ferne Geflohenen soll sie wie der Schlupfwinkel erscheinen, den er zu erreichen strebt. Unsere Feinde soll er, o Held, vollst├дndig, soll der Zersprenger vollst├дndig zersprengen.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдЬрдирд╛рдГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рдХрдердВ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддреЗрд░рдиреНрдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпреБрд╡рдореН) рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдореН (рддрдореН) (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдореЗрдШрд╛рд╡рд┐рд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреМ рд╕рднрд╛рд╕реЗрдиреЗрд╢реМ (рдкреБрд░реЛрдпреБрдзрд╛) рдкреБрд░рдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдВ рдпреБрдзреНрдпреЗрддреЗ рдпреМ рддреМ (рдпрдГ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдкреГрддрдиреНрдпрд╛рддреН) рдкреГрддрдирд╛рдВ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫреЗрддреН (рдЕрдк) (рддрдВрддрдореН) (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рд╣рддрдореН) рдирд╛рд╢рдпрддрдореН (рд╡рдЬреНрд░реЗрдг) рддреАрд╡реНрд░реЗрдг рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рд╜рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЗрдг (рддрдВрддрдореН) (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рд╣рддрдореН) (рджреВрд░реЗ) (рдЪрддреНрддрд╛рдп) рдпрд╛рдЪрд┐рддрд╛рдп (рдЫрдиреНрддреНрд╕рддреН) рд╕рдВрд╡реГрдгреБрдпрд╛рддреН (рдЧрд╣рдирдореН) рдХрдард┐рдирдореН (рдпрддреН) рдпрдГ (рдЗрдирдХреНрд╖рддреН) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН) (рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН) (рдкрд░рд┐) (рд╢реВрд░) (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддрдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ (рджрд░реНрдорд╛) рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░рдХрдГ рд╕рдиреН (рджрд░реНрд╖реАрд╖реНрдЯ) рджреГрдгреАрд╣рд┐ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддрдГ) рдЕрднрд┐рддрдГ рее рем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реИрд░реНрдпреЗ рд╕реЗрдиреЗрд╢рд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рд╢рддреНрд░рд╡рд╕реНрд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╕реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдордкрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░рд╡реЛ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднрд┐рдГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рднреЗрджрдордкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрддрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреАрд░реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрд░рдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддреБ рее рем реердЕрддреНрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдзрд░реНрдорд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрддреНрд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рдмреЛрдзреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореЗрдХрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╕реЗрдиреЗрддреАрд▓ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддреАрдЪреЗ рд╢рддреНрд░реВ рдЖрдкрд▓реЗ рд╢рддреНрд░реВ рд╕рдордЬрд▓реЗ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗрдд. рд╢рддреНрд░реВрддреАрд▓ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░ рднреЗрдж рдЬрд╛рдгреВрди рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдВрдиреА рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдВрдЪрд╛ рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░реВрди рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрдЪреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХреЗрд▓реЗ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ. рее рем рее
